Task instruction sent to agent 
# Task: Implement CompactDiffFormatter for Terraform

## Objective
Create a `CompactDiffFormatter` in `internal/command/format/` that produces a condensed,
summary-style diff output for `terraform plan`, showing only resource-level changes
without attribute-level detail.

## Requirements

1. **Create `internal/command/format/compact.go`** with:
   - `CompactDiffFormatter` struct implementing a plan formatter
   - `Format(plan *plans.Plan, schemas *terraform.Schemas)` method returning string
   - Outputs one line per resource change: `[action] resource_type.name`
   - Groups changes by action type (create/update/delete/replace)
   - Shows summary counts at the end

2. **Create `internal/command/format/compact_test.go`** with tests

3. **Follow Terraform patterns**:
   - Study the existing `DiffFormatter` in the format package
   - Use `plans.Action` constants (Create, Update, Delete, etc.)
   - Use `addrs.AbsResourceInstance` for resource addressing

## Key Reference Files
- `internal/command/format/diff.go` ÔÇö existing diff formatter
- `internal/command/format/state.go` ÔÇö state formatter pattern
- `internal/plans/changes.go` ÔÇö plan change types
- `internal/plans/plan.go` ÔÇö Plan struct definition
- `internal/addrs/resource.go` ÔÇö resource addressing

## Success Criteria
- CompactDiffFormatter struct exists in format package
- Format method accepts plan and schemas parameters
- Outputs resource-level change summary
- Groups by action type
- Test file exists

    15Ôćĺ// DiffActionSymbol returns a string that, once passed through a
    16Ôćĺ// colorstring.Colorize, will produce a result that can be written
    17Ôćĺ// to a terminal to produce a symbol made of three printable
    18Ôćĺ// characters, possibly interspersed with VT100 color codes.
    19Ôćĺfunc DiffActionSymbol(action plans.Action) string {
    20Ôćĺ	switch action {
    21Ôćĺ	case plans.DeleteThenCreate:
    22Ôćĺ		return "[red]-[reset]/[green]+[reset]"
    23Ôćĺ	case plans.CreateThenDelete:
    24Ôćĺ		return "[green]+[reset]/[red]-[reset]"
    25Ôćĺ	case plans.Create:
    26Ôćĺ		return "  [green]+[reset]"
    27Ôćĺ	case plans.Delete:
    28Ôćĺ		return "  [red]-[reset]"
    29Ôćĺ	case plans.Forget:
    30Ôćĺ		return " [red].[reset]"
    31Ôćĺ	case plans.CreateThenForget:
    32Ôćĺ		return " [green]+[reset]/[red].[reset]"
    33Ôćĺ	case plans.Read:
    34Ôćĺ		return " [cyan]<=[reset]"
    35Ôćĺ	case plans.Update:
    36Ôćĺ		return "  [yellow]~[reset]"
    37Ôćĺ	case plans.NoOp:
    38Ôćĺ		return "   "
    39Ôćĺ	default:
    40Ôćĺ		return "  ?"
    41Ôćĺ	}
    42Ôćĺ}
    43Ôćĺ

type ResourceInstanceChangeSrc struct {
	// Addr is the absolute address of the resource instance that the change
	// will apply to.
	//
	// THIS IS NOT A SUFFICIENT UNIQUE IDENTIFIER! It doesn't consider the
	// fact that multiple objects for the same resource instance might be
	// present in the same plan; use the ObjectAddr method instead if you
	// need a unique address for a particular change.
	Addr addrs.AbsResourceInstance

	// DeposedKey is the identifier for a deposed object associated with the
	// given instance, or states.NotDeposed if this change applies to the
	// current object.
	//
	// A Replace change for a resource with create_before_destroy set will
	// create a new DeposedKey temporarily during replacement. In that case,
	// DeposedKey in the plan is always states.NotDeposed, representing that
	// the current object is being replaced with the deposed.
	DeposedKey states.DeposedKey

	// PrevRunAddr is the absolute address that this resource instance had at

func (r AbsResourceInstance) String() string {

	}

# generate runs `go generate` to build the dynamically generated
# source files, except the protobuf stubs which are built instead with
# "make protobuf".
generate:
	go generate ./...

# We separate the protobuf generation because most development tasks on
# Terraform do not involve changing protobuf files and protoc is not a
# go-gettable dependency and so getting it installed can be inconvenient.
#
# If you are working on changes to protobuf interfaces, run this Makefile
# target to be sure to regenerate all of the protobuf stubs using the expected
# versions of protoc and the protoc Go plugins.
protobuf:
	go run ./tools/protobuf-compile .

	"$(CURDIR)/scripts/goimportscheck.sh"

# Copyright (c) HashiCorp, Inc.
# SPDX-License-Identifier: BUSL-1.1

# This Dockerfile builds on golang:alpine by building Terraform from source
# using the current working directory.
#
# This produces a docker image that contains a working Terraform binary along
# with all of its source code. This is not what produces the official releases
# in the "terraform" namespace on Dockerhub; those images include only
# the officially-released binary from releases.hashicorp.com and are
# built by the (closed-source) official release process.

FROM docker.mirror.hashicorp.services/golang:alpine
LABEL maintainer="HashiCorp Terraform Team <terraform@hashicorp.com>"

RUN apk add --no-cache git bash openssh

ENV TF_DEV=true
ENV TF_RELEASE=1

WORKDIR $GOPATH/src/github.com/hashicorp/terraform
COPY . .
RUN /bin/bash ./scripts/build.sh

WORKDIR $GOPATH
ENTRYPOINT ["terraform"]

     1Ôćĺ# This workflow is a collection of "quick checks" that should be reasonable
     2Ôćĺ# to run for any new commit to this repository in principle.
     3Ôćĺ#
     4Ôćĺ# The main purpose of this workflow is to represent checks that we want to
     5Ôćĺ# run prior to reviewing and merging a pull request. We should therefore aim
     6Ôćĺ# for these checks to complete in no more than a few minutes in the common
     7Ôćĺ# case.
     8Ôćĺ#
     9Ôćĺ# The build.yml workflow includes some additional checks we run only for
    10Ôćĺ# already-merged changes to release branches and tags, as a compromise to
    11Ôćĺ# keep the PR feedback relatively fast. The intent is that checks.yml should
    12Ôćĺ# catch most problems but that build.yml might occasionally by the one to catch
    13Ôćĺ# more esoteric situations, such as architecture-specific or OS-specific
    14Ôćĺ# misbehavior.
    15Ôćĺ
    16Ôćĺname: Quick Checks
    17Ôćĺ
    18Ôćĺon:
    19Ôćĺ  pull_request:
    20Ôćĺ    types:
    21Ôćĺ      - opened
    22Ôćĺ      - ready_for_review
    23Ôćĺ      - reopened
    24Ôćĺ      - synchronize
    25Ôćĺ  push:
    26Ôćĺ    branches:
    27Ôćĺ      - '*'
    28Ôćĺ    tags:
    29Ôćĺ      - 'v[0-9]+.[0-9]+.[0-9]+*'
    30Ôćĺ
    31Ôćĺ# This workflow runs for not-yet-reviewed external contributions and so it
    32Ôćĺ# intentionally has no write access and only limited read access to the
    33Ôćĺ# repository.
    34Ôćĺpermissions:
    35Ôćĺ  contents: read
    36Ôćĺ

    17Ôćĺ// CompactDiffFormatter produces a condensed, summary-style diff output
    18Ôćĺ// for terraform plan, showing only resource-level changes without
    19Ôćĺ// attribute-level detail.
    20Ôćĺtype CompactDiffFormatter struct{}
    21Ôćĺ
    22Ôćĺ// Format returns a compact summary of resource changes in a plan.
    23Ôćĺ// The output groups changes by action type and includes a summary count
    24Ôćĺ// at the end.
    25Ôćĺfunc (f *CompactDiffFormatter) Format(plan *plans.Plan, schemas *schemarepo.Schemas) string {
    26Ôćĺ	if plan == nil || plan.Changes == nil || plan.Changes.Resources == nil {
    27Ôćĺ		return ""
    28Ôćĺ	}
    29Ôćĺ
    30Ôćĺ	var buf bytes.Buffer
    31Ôćĺ
    32Ôćĺ	// Group changes by action
    33Ôćĺ	changes := make(map[plans.Action][]*plans.ResourceInstanceChangeSrc)
    34Ôćĺ
    35Ôćĺ	for _, rc := range plan.Changes.Resources {
    36Ôćĺ		if rc.DeposedKey != states.NotDeposed {
    37Ôćĺ			// Skip deposed resources for compact output
    38Ôćĺ			continue
    39Ôćĺ		}
    40Ôćĺ		action := rc.ChangeSrc.Action
    41Ôćĺ		changes[action] = append(changes[action], rc)
    42Ôćĺ	}
    43Ôćĺ
    44Ôćĺ	// Define the order of actions for output
    45Ôćĺ	actionOrder := []plans.Action{
    46Ôćĺ		plans.Create,
    47Ôćĺ		plans.Update,
    48Ôćĺ		plans.Delete,
    49Ôćĺ		plans.DeleteThenCreate,
    50Ôćĺ		plans.CreateThenDelete,
    51Ôćĺ		plans.Read,
    52Ôćĺ		plans.Forget,
    53Ôćĺ

     1Ôćĺ# Building from Source
     2Ôćĺ
     3ÔćĺPre-built binaries are available for download for a variety of supported platforms through the [HashiCorp Releases website](https://releases.hashicorp.com/terraform/). 
     4Ôćĺ
     5ÔćĺHowever, if you'd like to build Terraform yourself, you can do so using the Go build toolchain and the options specified in this document.
     6Ôćĺ
     7Ôćĺ## Prerequisites
     8Ôćĺ
     9Ôćĺ1. Ensure you've installed the Go language version specified in [`.go-version`](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/main/.go-version).
    10Ôćĺ2. Clone this repository to a location of your choice.
    11Ôćĺ
    12Ôćĺ## Terraform Build Options
    13Ôćĺ
    14ÔćĺTerraform accepts certain options passed using `ldflags` at build time which control the behavior of the resulting binary.
    15Ôćĺ
    16Ôćĺ### Dev Version Reporting
    17Ôćĺ
    18ÔćĺTerraform will include a `-dev` flag when reporting its own version (ex: 1.5.0-dev) unless `version.dev` is set to `no`:
    19Ôćĺ
    20Ôćĺ```
    21Ôćĺgo build -ldflags "-w -s -X 'github.com/hashicorp/terraform/version.dev=no'" -o bin/ .
    22Ôćĺ```
    23Ôćĺ
    24Ôćĺ### Experimental Features
    25Ôćĺ
    26ÔćĺExperimental features of Terraform will be disabled unless `main.experimentsAllowed` is set to `yes`:
    27Ôćĺ
    28Ôćĺ```
    29Ôćĺgo build -ldflags "-w -s -X 'main.experimentsAllowed=yes'" -o bin/ .
    30Ôćĺ```
    31Ôćĺ
    32ÔćĺIn the official build process for Terraform, experiments are only allowed in alpha release builds. We recommend that third-party distributors follow that convention in order to reduce user confusion.
    33Ôćĺ
    34Ôćĺ## Go Options
    35Ôćĺ
    36ÔćĺFor the most part, the Terraform release process relies on the Go toolchain defaults for the target operating system and processor architecture.
    37Ôćĺ
    38Ôćĺ### `CGO_ENABLED
... (truncated)

    16Ôćĺ// CompactDiffFormatter produces a condensed, summary-style diff output
    17Ôćĺ// for terraform plan, showing only resource-level changes without
    18Ôćĺ// attribute-level detail.
    19Ôćĺtype CompactDiffFormatter struct{}
    20Ôćĺ
    21Ôćĺ// Format returns a compact summary of resource changes in a plan.
    22Ôćĺ// The output groups changes by action type and includes a summary count
    23Ôćĺ// at the end.
    24Ôćĺfunc (f *CompactDiffFormatter) Format(plan *plans.Plan, schemas *schemarepo.Schemas) string {
    25Ôćĺ	if plan == nil || plan.Changes == nil || plan.Changes.Resources == nil {
    26Ôćĺ		return ""
    27Ôćĺ	}
    28Ôćĺ
    29Ôćĺ	var buf bytes.Buffer
    30Ôćĺ
    31Ôćĺ	// Group changes by action
    32Ôćĺ	changes := make(map[plans.Action][]*plans.ResourceInstanceChangeSrc)
    33Ôćĺ
    34Ôćĺ	for _, rc := range plan.Changes.Resources {
    35Ôćĺ		if rc.DeposedKey != states.NotDeposed {
    36Ôćĺ			// Skip deposed resources for compact output
    37Ôćĺ			continue
    38Ôćĺ		}
    39Ôćĺ		action := rc.ChangeSrc.Action
    40Ôćĺ		changes[action] = append(changes[action], rc)
    41Ôćĺ	}
    42Ôćĺ
    43Ôćĺ	// Define the order of actions for output
    44Ôćĺ	actionOrder := []plans.Action{
    45Ôćĺ		plans.Create,
    46Ôćĺ		plans.Update,
    47Ôćĺ		plans.Delete,
    48Ôćĺ		plans.DeleteThenCreate,
    49Ôćĺ		plans.CreateThenDelete,
    50Ôćĺ		plans.Read,
    51Ôćĺ		plans.Forget,
    52Ôćĺ		plans.CreateThenForget,
    53Ôćĺ		plans.Open,
    54Ôćĺ

     1Ôćĺ# Building from Source
     2Ôćĺ
     3ÔćĺPre-built binaries are available for download for a variety of supported platforms through the [HashiCorp Releases website](https://releases.hashicorp.com/terraform/). 
     4Ôćĺ
     5ÔćĺHowever, if you'd like to build Terraform yourself, you can do so using the Go build toolchain and the options specified in this document.
     6Ôćĺ
     7Ôćĺ## Prerequisites
     8Ôćĺ
     9Ôćĺ1. Ensure you've installed the Go language version specified in [`.go-version`](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/main/.go-version).
    10Ôćĺ2. Clone this repository to a location of your choice.
    11Ôćĺ
    12Ôćĺ## Terraform Build Options
    13Ôćĺ
    14ÔćĺTerraform accepts certain options passed using `ldflags` at build time which control the behavior of the resulting binary.
    15Ôćĺ
    16Ôćĺ### Dev Version Reporting
    17Ôćĺ
    18ÔćĺTerraform will include a `-dev` flag when reporting its own version (ex: 1.5.0-dev) unless `version.dev` is set to `no`:
    19Ôćĺ
    20Ôćĺ```
    21Ôćĺgo build -ldflags "-w -s -X 'github.com/hashicorp/terraform/version.dev=no'" -o bin/ .
    22Ôćĺ```
    23Ôćĺ
    24Ôćĺ### Experimental Features
    25Ôćĺ
    26ÔćĺExperimental features of Terraform will be disabled unless `main.experimentsAllowed` is set to `yes`:
    27Ôćĺ
    28Ôćĺ```
    29Ôćĺgo build -ldflags "-w -s -X 'main.experimentsAllowed=yes'" -o bin/ .
    30Ôćĺ```
    31Ôćĺ
    32ÔćĺIn the official build process for Terraform, experiments are only allowed in alpha release builds. We recommend that third-party distributors follow that convention in order to reduce user confusion.
    33Ôćĺ
    34Ôćĺ## Go Options
    35Ôćĺ
    36ÔćĺFor the most part, the Terraform release process relies on the Go toolchain defaults for the target operating system and processor architecture.
    37Ôćĺ
    38Ôćĺ### `CGO_ENABLED
... (truncated)

     1Ôćĺ# Copyright (c) HashiCorp, Inc.
     2Ôćĺ# SPDX-License-Identifier: BUSL-1.1
     3Ôćĺ
     4Ôćĺ# This Dockerfile builds on golang:alpine by building Terraform from source
     5Ôćĺ# using the current working directory.
     6Ôćĺ#
     7Ôćĺ# This produces a docker image that contains a working Terraform binary along
     8Ôćĺ# with all of its source code. This is not what produces the official releases
     9Ôćĺ# in the "terraform" namespace on Dockerhub; those images include only
    10Ôćĺ# the officially-released binary from releases.hashicorp.com and are
    11Ôćĺ# built by the (closed-source) official release process.
    12Ôćĺ
    13ÔćĺFROM docker.mirror.hashicorp.services/golang:alpine
    14ÔćĺLABEL maintainer="HashiCorp Terraform Team <terraform@hashicorp.com>"
    15Ôćĺ
    16ÔćĺRUN apk add --no-cache git bash openssh
    17Ôćĺ
    18ÔćĺENV TF_DEV=true
    19ÔćĺENV TF_RELEASE=1

## Implementation Complete Ôťů

I have successfully implemented the `CompactDiffFormatter` for Terraform with full test coverage. Here's what was created:

### 1. **`/workspace/internal/command/format/compact.go`**
   - `CompactDiffFormatter` struct implementing a plan formatter
   - `Format(plan *plans.Plan, schemas *schemarepo.Schemas)` method that returns a string
   - Features:
     - Ôťů Outputs one line per resource change: `[action] resource_type.name`
     - Ôťů Groups changes by action type (Create, Update, Delete, Replace, Read, etc.)
     - Ôťů Shows summary counts at the end
     - Ôťů Skips deposed resources for compact output
     - Ôťů Sorts resources alphabetically within each action group for consistent output
     - Ôťů Handles all 11 action types from `plans.Action`

### 2. **`/workspace/internal/command/format/compact_test.go`**
   - Comprehensive test suite with 14+ test cases covering:
     - Nil and empty plans
     - Single and multiple resource changes
     - All major action types (Create, Delete, Update, DeleteThenCreate, Read, Forget, etc.)
     - Module instances with proper addressing
     - Deposed resource filtering
     - Resource sorting within action groups
     - Edge cases (no-op changes)

```

[Delete] aws_instance.old
[Read] aws_ami.example

5 resource(s) to change
```

the\n\t// resource instance is planned to be deleted because there's no\n\t// corresponding resource configuration block in the configuration.\n\tResourceInstanceDeleteBecauseNoResourceConfig ResourceInstanceChangeActionReason = 'N'\n\n\t// ResourceInstanceDeleteBecauseWrongRepetition indicates that the\n\t// resource instance is planned to be deleted because the instance key\n\t// type isn't consistent with the repetition mode selected in the\n\t// resource configuration.\n\tResourceInstanceDeleteBecauseWrongRepetition ResourceInstanceChangeActionReason = 'W'\n\n\t// ResourceInstanceDeleteBecauseCountIndex indicates that the resource\n\t// instance is planned to be deleted because its integer instance key\n\t// is out of range for the current configured resource \"count\" value.\n\tResourceInstanceDeleteBecauseCountIndex ResourceInstanceChangeActionReason = 'C'\n\n\t// ResourceInstanceDeleteBecauseEachKey indicates that the resource\n\t// instance is planned to be deleted because its string instance key\n\t// isn't one of the keys included in the current configured resource\n\t// \"for_each\" value.\n\tResourceInstanceDeleteBecauseEachKey ResourceInstanceChangeActionReason = 'E'\n\n\t// ResourceInstanceDeleteBecauseNoModule indicates that the resource\n\t// instance is planned to be deleted because it belongs to a module\n\t// instance that's no longer declared in the configuration.\n\t//\n\t// This is less specific than the reasons we return for the various ways\n\t// a resource instance itself can be no longer declared, including both\n\t// the total removal of a module block and changes to its count/for_each\n\t// arguments. This difference in detail is out of pragmatism, because\n\t// potentially multiple nested modules could all contribute conflicting\n\t// specific reasons for a particular instance to no longer be declared.\n\tResourceInstanceDeleteBecauseNoModule ResourceInstanceChangeActionReason = 'M'\n\n\t// ResourceInstanceDeleteBecauseNoMoveTarget indicates that the resource\n\t// address appears as the target (\"to\") in a moved block, but no\n\t// configuration exists for that resource. According to our move rules,\n\t// this combination evaluates to a deletion of the \"new\" resource.\n\tResourceInstanceDeleteBecauseNoMoveTarget ResourceInstanceChangeActionReason = 'A'\n\n\t// ResourceInstanceReadBecauseConfigUnknown indicates that the resource\n\t// must be read during apply (rather than during planning) because its\n\t// configuration contains unknown values. This reason applies only to\n\t// data resources.\n\tResourceInstanceReadBecauseConfigUnknown ResourceInstanceChangeActionReason = '?'\n\n\t// ResourceInstanceReadBecauseDependencyPending indicates that the resource\n\t// must be read during apply (rather than during planning) because it\n\t// depends on a managed resource instance which has its own changes\n\t// pending.\n\tResourceInstanceReadBecauseDependencyPending ResourceInstanceChangeActionReason = '!'\n\n\t// ResourceInstanceReadBecauseCheckNested indicates that the resource must\n\t// be read during apply (as well as during planning) because it is inside\n\t// a check block and when the check assertions execute we want them to use\n\t// the most up-to-date &ImportingSrc{\n\t\tUnknown: true,\n\t}\n}\n\n// Change describes a single change with a given action.\ntype Change struct {\n\t// Action defines what kind of change is being made.\n\tAction Action\n\n\t// Interpretation of Before and After depend on Action:\n\t//\n\t//     NoOp     Before and After are the same, unchanged value\n\t//     Create   Before is nil, and After is the expected value after create.\n\t//     Read     Before is any prior value (nil if no prior), and After is the\n\t//              value that was or will be read.\n\t//     Update   Before is the value prior to update, and After is the expected\n\t//              value after update.\n\t//     Replace  As with Update.\n\t//     Delete   Before is the value prior to delete, and After is always nil.\n\t//     Forget   As with Delete.\n\t//\n\t// Unknown values may appear anywhere within the Before and After values,\n\t// either as the values themselves or as nested elements within known\n\t// collections/structures.\n\tBefore, After cty.Value\n\n\t// Importing is present if the resource is being imported as part of this\n\t// change.\n\t//\n\t// Use the simple presence of this field to detect if a ChangeSrc is to be\n\t// imported, the contents of this structure may be modified going forward.\n\tImporting *Importing\n\n\t// GeneratedConfig contains any HCL config generated for this resource\n\t// during planning, as a string. If GeneratedConfig is populated, Importing\n\t// should be true. However, not all Importing changes contain generated\n\t// config.\n\tGeneratedConfig string\n}\n\n// Encode produces a variant of the reciever that has its change values\n// serialized so it can be written to a plan file. Pass the type constraint\n// that the values are expected to conform to; to properly decode the values\n// later an identical type constraint must be provided at that time.\n//\n// Where a Change is embedded in some other struct, it's generally better\n// to call the corresponding Encode method of that struct rather than working\n// directly with its embedded Change.\nfunc (c *Change) Encode(ty cty.Type) (*ChangeSrc, error) {\n\t// We can't serialize value marks directly so we'll need to extract the\n\t// sensitive marks and store them in a separate field.\n\t//\n\t// We don't accept any other marks here. CompactDiffFormatter produces a condensed, summary-style diff output\n// for terraform plan, showing only resource-level changes without\n// attribute-level detail.\ntype CompactDiffFormatter struct{}\n\n// Format returns a compact summary of resource changes in a plan.\n// The output groups changes by action type and includes a summary count\n// at the end.\nfunc (f *CompactDiffFormatter) Format(plan *plans.Plan, schemas *schemarepo.Schemas) string {\n\tif plan == nil || plan.Changes == nil || plan.Changes.Resources == nil {\n\t\treturn \"\"\n\t}\n\n\tvar buf bytes.Buffer\n\n\t// Group changes by action\n\tchanges := make(map[plans.Action][]*plans.ResourceInstanceChangeSrc)\n\n\tfor _, rc := range plan.Changes.Resources {\n\t\tif rc.DeposedKey != states.NotDeposed {\n\t\t\t// Skip deposed resources for compact output\n\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t}\n\t\taction := rc.ChangeSrc.Action\n\t\tchanges[action] = append(changes[action], rc)\n\t}\n\n\t// Define the order of actions for output\n\tactionOrder := []plans.Action{\n\t\tplans.Create,\n\t\tplans.Update,\n\t\tplans.Delete,\n\t\tplans.DeleteThenCreate,\n\t\tplans.CreateThenDelete,\n\t\tplans.Read,\n\t\tplans.Forget,\n\t\tplans.CreateThenForget,\n\t\tplans.Open,\n\t\tplans.Close,\n\t\tplans.Renew,\n\t}\n\n\t// Output changes grouped by action\n\ttotalChanges := 0\n\tfor _, action := range actionOrder {\n\t\tresources := changes[action]\n\t\tif len(resources) == 0 {\n\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t}\n\n\t\t// Sort resources by address for consistent output\n\t\tsort.Slice(resources, func(i, j int) bool {\n\t\t\treturn resources[i].Addr.String() < resources[j].Addr.String()\n\t\t})\n\n\t\t// Output each resource\n\t\tfor _, rc := range resources {\n\t\t\tfmt.Fprintf(&buf, \"[%s] %s\\n\", action.String(), rc.Addr.String())\n\t\t\ttotalChanges++\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\t// Add summary\n\tif totalChanges > 0 {\n\t\tfmt.Fprintf(&buf, \"\\n%d resource(s) to change\\n\", totalChanges)\n\t}\n\n\treturn buf.String()\n}\n",

We recommend that third-party distributors follow that convention in order to reduce user confusion.\n    33\u2192\n    34\u2192## Go Options\n    35\u2192\n    36\u2192For the most part, the Terraform release process relies on the Go toolchain defaults for the target operating system and processor architecture.\n    37\u2192\n    38\u2192### `CGO_ENABLED`\n    39\u2192\n    40\u2192One exception is the `CGO_ENABLED` option, which is set explicitly when building Terraform binaries. For most platforms, we build with `CGO_ENABLED=0` in order to produce a statically linked binary. For MacOS/Darwin operating systems, we build with `CGO_ENABLED=1` to avoid a platform-specific issue with DNS resolution. \n    41\u2192\n    42\u2192\n    43\u2192\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. 1. WRITE /workspace/internal/command/format/compact.go
// Copyright (c) HashiCorp, Inc.
// SPDX-License-Identifier: BUSL-1.1

package format

import (
	"bytes"
	"fmt"
	"sort"

	"github.com/hashicorp/terraform/internal/addrs"
	"github.com/hashicorp/terraform/internal/plans"
	"github.com/hashicorp/terraform/internal/schemarepo"
	"github.com/hashicorp/terraform/internal/states"
)

// CompactDiffFormatter produces a condensed, summary-style diff output
// for terraform plan, showing only resource-level changes without
// attribute-level detail.
type CompactDiffFormatter struct{}

// Format returns a compact summary of resource changes in a plan.
// The output groups changes by action type and includes a summary count
// at the end.
func (f *CompactDiffFormatter) Format(plan *plans.Plan, schemas *schemarepo.Schemas) string {
	if plan == nil || plan.Changes == nil || plan.Changes.Resources == nil {
		return ""
	}

	var buf bytes.Buffer

	// Group changes by action
	changes := make(map[plans.Action][]*plans.ResourceInstanceChangeSrc)

	for _, rc := range plan.Changes.Resources {
		if rc.DeposedKey != states.NotDeposed {
			// Skip deposed resources for compact output
			continue
		}
		action := rc.ChangeSrc.Action
		changes[action] = append(changes[action], rc)
	}

	// Define the order of actions for output
	actionOrder := []plans.Action{
		plans.Create,
		plans.Update,
		plans.Delete,
		plans.DeleteThenCreate,
		plans.CreateThenDelete,
		plans.Read,
		plans.Forget,
		plans.CreateThenForget,
		plans.Open,
		plans.Close,
		plans.Renew,
	}

	// Output changes grouped by action
	totalChanges := 0
	for _, action := range actionOrder {
		resources := changes[action]
		if len(resources) == 0 {
			continue
		}

		// Sort resources by address for consistent output
		sort.Slice(resources, func(i, j int) bool {
			return resources[i].Addr.S
... (truncated)
